 199:     generate_report: generateReport,
 200:     report_port: reportPort,
 201:     raw_upload_permission: rawUploadPermission,
 202:   })
 203: 
 204:   const project = findProjectForPath(updated, root)
 205:   if (!project) {
 206:     process.stderr.write(`Failed to register project: ${root}\n`)
 207:     return 1
 208:   }
 209: 
 210:   const worktree = ensureProjectWorktree(project)
 211:   saveConfig(updated)
 212:   let upstream: ReturnType<typeof ensureBranchUpstream> | null = null
 213:   let upstreamError = ''
 214:   if (project.auto_push) {
 215:     try {
 216:       upstream = ensureBranchUpstream(project.memory_path, worktree.branch)
 217:     } catch (error: unknown) {
 218:       upstreamError = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
 219:     }
 220:   }
 221: 
 222:   process.stdout.write(`Registered project: ${project.name}\n`)
 223:   process.stdout.write(`Development path: ${project.development_path}\n`)
 224:   process.stdout.write(`Memory path: ${project.memory_path}\n`)
 225:   process.stdout.write(`Memory branch: ${project.memory_branch}\n`)
 226:   process.stdout.write(`Heartbeat interval: ${project.heartbeat_interval}\n`)
 227:   process.stdout.write(`Auto-push: ${project.auto_push}\n`)
 228:   process.stdout.write(`Generate report: ${project.generate_report}\n`)
 229:   process.stdout.write(`Raw upload permission: ${project.raw_upload_permission}\n`)
 230:   process.stdout.write(`Worktree branch: ${worktree.branch}\n`)
 231:   process.stdout.write(`Worktree created: ${worktree.created ? 'yes' : 'no'}\n`)
 232:   if (upstreamError) {
 233:     process.stderr.write(`Upstream configured: failed (${upstreamError})\n`)
 234:   } else if (upstream === null) {
 235:     process.stdout.write('Upstream configured: skipped (auto_push disabled)\n')
 236:   } else if (upstream.remote === null) {
 237:     process.stdout.write('Upstream configured: no remote available\n')
 238:   } else {
 239:     process.stdout.write(`Upstream configured: ${upstream.created ? 'yes' : 'already'} (${upstream.remote}/${worktree.branch})\n`)
 240:   }
 241:   return upstreamError ? 1 : 0
 242: }
 243: 
 244: function parseRawUploadPermissionOption(value: string): 'not-set' | 'approved' | 'denied' | null {
 245:   const normalized = normalizeRawUploadPermission(value, DEFAULT_RAW_UPLOAD_PERMISSION)
 246:   return normalized === DEFAULT_RAW_UPLOAD_PERMISSION && value.trim().toLowerCase() !== DEFAULT_RAW_UPLOAD_PERMISSION
 247:     ? null
 248:     : normalized
 249: }
 250: 
 251: export async function cmdQuickStart(options: {
 252:   root: string
 253:   name?: string
 254: }): Promise<number> {
 255:   const root = resolve(options.root)
 256:   const config = loadConfig()
 257:   const quickStartSeconds = intervalToSeconds(QUICK_START_HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL)
 258:   const schedulerIntervalSeconds = registeredHeartbeatIntervalSeconds()
 259:   const effectiveSchedulerSeconds = schedulerIntervalSeconds ?? intervalToSeconds(config.heartbeat_interval)
 260:   const effectiveSchedulerLabel = schedulerIntervalSeconds === null
 261:     ? config.heartbeat_interval
 262:     : formatIntervalSeconds(schedulerIntervalSeconds)
 263: 
 264:   process.stdout.write('Quick Start: prepare scheduler, register this repository in the single-source memory flow, and run one sync now.\n')
 265: 
 266:   if (!isHeartbeatRegistered()) {
 267:     process.stdout.write('Step 1/3: installing heartbeat scheduler with recommended defaults.\n')
 268:     const installResult = cmdInstall({ interval: QUICK_START_HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL, autoPush: 'true' })
 269:     if (installResult !== 0) {
 270:       return installResult
 271:     }
 272:   } else if (effectiveSchedulerSeconds > quickStartSeconds) {
 273:     process.stdout.write(
 274:       `Step 1/3: heartbeat scheduler is registered at ${effectiveSchedulerLabel}; ` +
 275:       `reinstalling it to ${QUICK_START_HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL} so Quick Start can run on time.\n`,
 276:     )
 277:     const uninstallResult = cmdUninstall()
 278:     if (uninstallResult !== 0) {
 279:       return uninstallResult
 280:     }
 281: 
 282:     const installResult = cmdInstall({
 283:       interval: QUICK_START_HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL,
 284:       autoPush: config.auto_push ? 'true' : 'false',
 285:     })
 286:     if (installResult !== 0) {
 287:       return installResult
 288:     }
 289:   } else {
 290:     process.stdout.write(
 291:       `Step 1/3: heartbeat scheduler already registered at ${effectiveSchedulerLabel}; keeping the existing install.\n`,
 292:     )
 293:   }
 294: 
 295:   process.stdout.write('Step 2/3: registering the current repository with Quick Start settings.\n')
 296:   const registerOptions: Parameters<typeof cmdRegisterProject>[0] = {
 297:     root,
 298:     quickStart: true,
 299:   }
 300:   if (options.name !== undefined) {
 301:     registerOptions.name = options.name
 302:   }
 303: 
 304:   const registerResult = cmdRegisterProject(registerOptions)
 305:   if (registerResult !== 0) {
 306:     return registerResult
 307:   }
 308: 
 309:   process.stdout.write('Step 3/3: running one immediate heartbeat sync.\n')
 310:   return await cmdRunOnce({
 311:     root,
 312:     force: true,
 313:   })
 314: }
 315: 
 316: export function registeredHeartbeatIntervalSeconds(): number | null {
 317:   const sys = platform
 318:   if (sys === 'linux') return cronRegisteredIntervalSeconds()
 319:   if (sys === 'darwin') return launchdRegisteredIntervalSeconds()
 320:   if (sys === 'win32') return schtasksRegisteredIntervalSeconds()
 321:   return null
 322: }
 323: 
 324: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 325: // Linux (cron)
 326: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 327: 
 328: function installCron(scriptPath: string, seconds: number): number {
 329:   if (isCronRegistered()) {
 330:     process.stderr.write("Heartbeat is already registered in cron. Use 'uninstall' first.\n")
 331:     return 1
 332:   }
 333: 
 334:   const minutes = Math.max(1, Math.floor(seconds / 60))
 335:   const logDir = resolve(homedir(), '.memorytree', 'logs')
 336:   mkdirSync(logDir, { recursive: true })
 337: 
 338:   const cronLine = `*/${minutes} * * * * node "${scriptPath}" daemon run-once >> "${resolve(logDir, 'heartbeat-cron.log')}" 2>&1 # memorytree`
 339:   const existing = getCrontab()
 340:   const newCrontab = existing.trim()
 341:     ? existing.trimEnd() + '\n' + cronLine + '\n'
 342:     : cronLine + '\n'
 343: 
 344:   try {
 345:     const tmpFile = resolve(homedir(), '.memorytree', '.crontab.tmp')
 346:     writeFileSync(tmpFile, newCrontab)
 347:     execCommand('crontab', [tmpFile])
 348:     unlinkSync(tmpFile)
 349:   } catch {
 350:     process.stderr.write('Failed to install cron job.\n')
 351:     return 1
 352:   }
 353: 
 354:   process.stdout.write(`Heartbeat registered in cron (every ${minutes}m).\n`)
 355:   return 0
 356: }
 357: 
 358: function uninstallCron(): number {
 359:   const existing = getCrontab()
 360:   const filtered = existing.split('\n').filter(line => !line.includes('memorytree')).join('\n') + '\n'
 361:   try {
 362:     const tmpFile = resolve(homedir(), '.memorytree', '.crontab.tmp')
 363:     mkdirSync(dirname(tmpFile), { recursive: true })
 364:     writeFileSync(tmpFile, filtered)
 365:     execCommand('crontab', [tmpFile])
 366:     unlinkSync(tmpFile)
 367:   } catch {
 368:     // best effort
 369:   }
 370:   process.stdout.write('Heartbeat removed from cron.\n')
 371:   return 0
 372: }
 373: 
 374: export function isCronRegistered(): boolean {
 375:   return getCrontab().includes('memorytree')
 376: }
 377: 
 378: function getCrontab(): string {
 379:   try {
 380:     return execCommand('crontab', ['-l'], { allowFailure: true })
 381:   } catch {
 382:     return ''
 383:   }
 384: }
 385: 
 386: function cronRegisteredIntervalSeconds(): number | null {
 387:   const line = getCrontab()
 388:     .split(/\r?\n/)
 389:     .find(candidate => candidate.includes('memorytree'))
 390:   if (!line) return null
 391: 
 392:   const match = line.match(/^\*\/(\d+)\s+\*\s+\*\s+\*\s+\*.*#\s*memorytree\s*$/)
 393:   if (!match) return null
 394: 
 395:   const minutes = parseInt(match[1]!, 10)
 396:   return Number.isInteger(minutes) && minutes > 0 ? minutes * 60 : null
 397: }
 398: 
 399: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 400: // macOS (launchd)
 401: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 402: 
 403: function launchdPlistPath(): string {
 404:   return resolve(homedir(), 'Library', 'LaunchAgents', `${LAUNCHD_LABEL}.plist`)
 405: }
 406: 
 407: function installLaunchd(scriptPath: string, seconds: number): number {
 408:   const plistPath = launchdPlistPath()
 409:   if (existsSync(plistPath)) {
 410:     process.stderr.write("Heartbeat plist already exists. Use 'uninstall' first.\n")
 411:     return 1
 412:   }
 413: 
 414:   const logDir = resolve(homedir(), '.memorytree', 'logs')
 415:   mkdirSync(logDir, { recursive: true })
 416: 
 417:   const plistContent = `<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
 418: <!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC "-//Apple//DTD PLIST 1.0//EN" "http://www.apple.com/DTDs/PropertyList-1.0.dtd">
 419: <plist version="1.0">
 420: <dict>
 421:     <key>Label</key>
 422:     <string>${LAUNCHD_LABEL}</string>
 423:     <key>ProgramArguments</key>
 424:     <array>
 425:         <string>node</string>
 426:         <string>${scriptPath}</string>
 427:         <string>daemon</string>
 428:         <string>run-once</string>
 429:     </array>
 430:     <key>StartInterval</key>
 431:     <integer>${seconds}</integer>
 432:     <key>StandardOutPath</key>
 433:     <string>${resolve(logDir, 'heartbeat-launchd.log')}</string>
 434:     <key>StandardErrorPath</key>
 435:     <string>${resolve(logDir, 'heartbeat-launchd.log')}</string>
 436: </dict>
 437: </plist>
 438: `
 439:   mkdirSync(dirname(plistPath), { recursive: true })
 440:   writeFileSync(plistPath, plistContent, 'utf-8')
 441: 
 442:   try {
 443:     execCommand('launchctl', ['load', plistPath])
 444:   } catch {
 445:     process.stderr.write('Failed to load plist.\n')
 446:     return 1
 447:   }
 448: 
 449:   process.stdout.write(`Heartbeat registered via launchd (every ${seconds}s).\n`)
 450:   return 0
 451: }
 452: 
 453: function uninstallLaunchd(): number {
 454:   const plistPath = launchdPlistPath()
 455:   if (existsSync(plistPath)) {
 456:     try { execCommand('launchctl', ['unload', plistPath], { allowFailure: true }) } catch { /* ignore */ }
 457:     try { unlinkSync(plistPath) } catch { /* ignore */ }
 458:   }
 459:   process.stdout.write('Heartbeat removed from launchd.\n')
 460:   return 0
 461: }
 462: 
 463: export function isLaunchdRegistered(): boolean {
 464:   return existsSync(launchdPlistPath())
 465: }
 466: 
 467: function launchdRegisteredIntervalSeconds(): number | null {
 468:   const plistPath = launchdPlistPath()
 469:   if (!existsSync(plistPath)) return null
 470: 
 471:   try {
 472:     const text = readFileSync(plistPath, 'utf-8')
 473:     const match = text.match(/<key>StartInterval<\/key>\s*<integer>(\d+)<\/integer>/i)
 474:     if (!match) return null
 475: 
 476:     const seconds = parseInt(match[1]!, 10)
 477:     return Number.isInteger(seconds) && seconds > 0 ? seconds : null
 478:   } catch {
 479:     return null
 480:   }
 481: }
 482: 
 483: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 484: // Windows (Task Scheduler)
 485: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 486: 
 487: // Write a VBScript launcher that runs node silently (no console window).
 488: // wscript.exe /B runs in batch mode (suppresses script error popups).
 489: // VBScript Run(..., 0, False): 0 = SW_HIDE hides the window; False = fire-and-forget.
 490: // Written as UTF-16 LE with BOM so wscript.exe handles non-ASCII paths (e.g. Chinese
 491: // usernames) correctly on all Windows versions.
 492: export function vbsLauncherPath(): string {
 493:   return resolve(homedir(), '.memorytree', 'heartbeat-launcher.vbs')
 494: }
 495: 
 496: export function writeVbsLauncher(scriptPath: string): string {
 497:   const vbsPath = vbsLauncherPath()
 498:   mkdirSync(dirname(vbsPath), { recursive: true })
 499:   // Inside VBScript strings, double-quote is escaped as ""
 500:   const escapedScript = scriptPath.replace(/"/g, '""')
 501:   // Use the full node binary path so the launcher works even when Task Scheduler's
 502:   // PATH differs from the user's shell (e.g. nvm/fnm environments).
 503:   const escapedNode = process.execPath.replace(/"/g, '""')
 504:   const content = [
 505:     'Set WshShell = CreateObject("WScript.Shell")',
 506:     `WshShell.Run """${escapedNode}"" ""${escapedScript}"" daemon run-once", 0, False`,
 507:   ].join('\r\n') + '\r\n'
 508:   // UTF-16 LE BOM: recognised by wscript.exe on all Windows versions and preserves
 509:   // non-ASCII characters (e.g. Chinese home directory paths) without corruption.
 510:   const buf = Buffer.concat([Buffer.from([0xff, 0xfe]), Buffer.from(content, 'utf16le')])
 511:   writeFileSync(vbsPath, buf)
 512:   return vbsPath
 513: }
 514: 
 515: function installSchtasks(scriptPath: string, seconds: number): number {
 516:   if (isSchtasksRegistered()) {
 517:     process.stderr.write("Heartbeat is already registered in Task Scheduler. Use 'uninstall' first.\n")
 518:     return 1
 519:   }
 520: 
 521:   const minutes = Math.max(1, Math.floor(seconds / 60))
 522:   const vbsPath = writeVbsLauncher(scriptPath)
 523:   const trCommand = `wscript.exe /B "${vbsPath}"`
 524: 
 525:   try {
 526:     execCommand('schtasks', [
 527:       '/create', '/tn', TASK_NAME, '/sc', 'minute', '/mo', String(minutes),
 528:       '/tr', trCommand, '/f',
 529:     ])
 530:   } catch {
 531:     // schtasks failed — remove the launcher file we just wrote to keep state clean
 532:     try { unlinkSync(vbsPath) } catch { /* ignore */ }
 533:     process.stderr.write('Failed to create scheduled task.\n')
 534:     return 1
 535:   }
 536: 
 537:   process.stdout.write(`Heartbeat registered in Task Scheduler (every ${minutes}m).\n`)
 538:   return 0
 539: }
 540: 
 541: function uninstallSchtasks(): number {
 542:   try {
 543:     execCommand('schtasks', ['/delete', '/tn', TASK_NAME, '/f'], { allowFailure: true })
 544:   } catch {
 545:     // best effort
 546:   }
 547:   const vbsPath = vbsLauncherPath()
 548:   if (existsSync(vbsPath)) {
 549:     try { unlinkSync(vbsPath) } catch { /* ignore */ }
 550:   }
 551:   process.stdout.write('Heartbeat removed from Task Scheduler.\n')
 552:   return 0
 553: }
 554: 
 555: export function isSchtasksRegistered(): boolean {
 556:   try {
 557:     execCommand('schtasks', ['/query', '/tn', TASK_NAME])
 558:     return true
 559:   } catch {
 560:     return false
 561:   }
 562: }
 563: 
 564: function schtasksRegisteredIntervalSeconds(): number | null {
 565:   try {
 566:     const xml = execCommand('schtasks', ['/query', '/tn', TASK_NAME, '/xml'], { allowFailure: true })
 567:     if (!xml.trim()) return null
 568: 
 569:     const match = xml.match(/<Interval>([^<]+)<\/Interval>/i)
 570:     if (!match) return null
 571: 
 572:     return parseIsoDurationToSeconds(match[1]!)
 573:   } catch {
 574:     return null
 575:   }
 576: }
 577: 
 578: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 579: // Helpers
 580: // ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 581: 
 582: export function heartbeatScriptPath(): string {
 583:   // Use process.argv[1] which is the actual script being executed,
 584:   // more reliable than import.meta.url which varies between tsx and bundled output
 585:   const scriptArg = process.argv[1] ?? ''
 586:   if (scriptArg && scriptArg.endsWith('cli.js')) {
 587:     return resolve(scriptArg)
 588:   }
 589:   return fallbackHeartbeatScriptPath(import.meta.url)
 590: }
 591: 
 592: export function fallbackHeartbeatScriptPath(moduleUrl: string): string {
 593:   const moduleDir = dirname(fileURLToPath(moduleUrl))
 594:   if (basename(moduleDir).toLowerCase() === 'dist') {
 595:     return resolve(moduleDir, 'cli.js')
 596:   }
 597:   return resolve(moduleDir, '..', '..', 'dist', 'cli.js')
 598: }
 599: 
 600: function parseOptionalBoolean(value: string | undefined): boolean | undefined {
 601:   if (value === undefined) return undefined
 602:   if (value === 'true') return true
 603:   if (value === 'false') return false
 604:   return undefined
 605: }
 606: 
 607: function parseIsoDurationToSeconds(value: string): number | null {
 608:   const match = value.trim().match(/^P(?:(\d+)D)?(?:T(?:(\d+)H)?(?:(\d+)M)?(?:(\d+)S)?)?$/i)
 609:   if (!match) return null
 610: 
 611:   const days = parseInt(match[1] ?? '0', 10)
 612:   const hours = parseInt(match[2] ?? '0', 10)
 613:   const minutes = parseInt(match[3] ?? '0', 10)
 614:   const seconds = parseInt(match[4] ?? '0', 10)
 615:   const total = (days * 86400) + (hours * 3600) + (minutes * 60) + seconds
 616:   return total > 0 ? total : null
 617: }
 618: 
 619: function formatIntervalSeconds(seconds: number): string {
 620:   if (seconds % 3600 === 0) return `${String(seconds / 3600)}h`
 621:   if (seconds % 60 === 0) return `${String(seconds / 60)}m`
 622:   return `${String(seconds)}s`
 623: }

   2:

   5: ## Safe Defaults
   6: 
   7: - Do not mix MemoryTree-owned changes with product code changes by default.
   8: - Do not stage or push unrelated user work.
   9: - Do not assume direct commits to protected branches are allowed.
  10: - Do not bypass review, CI, E2E, or release controls.
  11: - Do not modify the host repository's CI, E2E, branch protection, or required-check configuration by default.
  12: - Keep raw transcript files in the current project's transcript mirror by default, but exclude them from automatic staging unless the user explicitly approved raw transcript uploads for the current repository.
  13: - Do not mirror or stage transcript files from unrelated projects inside the current repository.
  14: 
  15: ## Policy Merge
  16: 
  17: When the repo already has branch or PR rules:
  18: 
  19: 1. Keep the repo's stricter rule.
  20: 2. Treat MemoryTree as documentation and process support.
  21: 3. Only add MemoryTree-specific guidance that does not weaken repo controls.
  22: 
  23: ## MemoryTree-Owned Files
  24: 
  25: Default whitelist:
  26: 
  27: - `Memory/**`, except `Memory/06_transcripts/raw/**` until the user explicitly approved raw transcript uploads for this repository
  28: - `AGENTS.md` only when the file is managed by MemoryTree or the user approved the merge
  29: 
  30: If the diff includes files outside this whitelist, stop and ask before staging or pushing.
  31: 
  32: ## Default MemoryTree Flow
  33: 
  34: Use this flow only for MemoryTree-only changes and only when the host repo does not forbid it:
  35: 
  36: 1. Stage only the MemoryTree-owned files created or updated by the skill.
  37: 2. Create or reuse a dedicated branch such as `memorytree/<scope>-<yyyymmdd>-<slug>`.
  38: 3. Use a MemoryTree-scoped commit title. Prefer `memorytree(<scope>): <subject>`, but if the host repo enforces a commit convention, use a compatible equivalent such as `docs(memorytree): <subject>`.
  39: 4. Push that dedicated branch if the repository allows the current actor to push.
  40: 5. Open a dedicated PR instead of merging directly into a protected branch.
  41: 6. Enable auto-merge only when the repository still enforces its required approvals and checks.
  42: 7. If transcript files are included, keep the PR scoped to one repository's transcript mirror only. Do not mix cross-project transcript archives into the same PR.
  43: 8. Keep the global transcript archive updated in the same import operation, but never stage or push that user-level global archive as part of a repo PR.
  44: 
  45: ## Auto Push
  46: 
  47: When `auto_push = true` in `~/.memorytree/config.toml`:
  48: 
  49: 1. The heartbeat process pushes the current branch after each commit.
  50: 2. Before pushing, verify that a Git remote is configured. If no remote exists, skip the push and write an alert to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`.
  51: 3. If a push fails (network, authentication, rejected by server), retry once. On second failure, write an alert and continue to the next project.
  52: 4. On the very first push for a newly registered project, confirm with the user that the remote and branch are correct.
  53: 5. Do not force-push. Use only fast-forward pushes.
  54: 
  55: When `auto_push = false`:
  56: 
  57: 1. The heartbeat commits locally but does not push.
  58: 2. The user pushes manually or through the interactive skill session.
  59: 
  60: Rationale: project memory is a user asset. Local-only storage risks data loss from hardware failure or accidental deletion. Automatic push to a remote provides a durable backup.
  61: 
  62: ## Historical Exposure Boundary
  63: 
  64: - The single-source rollout is future-facing by default. De-tracked cache mirrors and raw-upload approval rules reduce future exposure, but they do not rewrite older Git history.
  65: - Do not rewrite history or force-push by default just because older commits once tracked `AGENTS.md` or `Memory/**`.
  66: - If older reachable history is confirmed to contain live credentials, regulated personal data, or other content that must be purged, treat it as a security or compliance incident rather than routine MemoryTree cleanup.
  67: 
  68: Recommended incident order:
  69: 
  70: 1. Revoke or rotate exposed credentials first.
  71: 2. Pause new MemoryTree pushes or PRs that would continue spreading the affected mirror paths.
  72: 3. Assess the full reachability scope: protected branches, open branches, tags, releases, workflow artifacts, and known forks.
  73: 4. Rewrite history only with repository-owner approval and coordinated collaborator communication.
  74: 5. After cleanup, re-check `.gitignore`, de-track state, and raw transcript upload policy so the same exposure path does not reopen.
  75: 
  76: ## Commit Guidance
  77: 
  78: - Keep the title concise and specific.
  79: - Prefer scopes such as `agents`, `goals`, `todos`, `chat-logs`, `transcripts`, `knowledge`, `archive`, `policy`, or `bootstrap`.
  80: - If a body is needed, keep it lightweight: reason, affected files, and whether the change is MemoryTree-only.
  81: - If the host repo requires Conventional Commits or another enforced prefix, keep `memorytree` visible as the scope or memory tag rather than bypassing the repo rule.
  82: 
  83: Example title:
  84: 
  85: ```text
  86: memorytree(todos): sync active todo progress
  87: ```
  88: 
  89: Host-compatible example:
  90: 
  91: ```text
  92: docs(memorytree): sync active todo progress
  93: ```
  94: 
  95: Example body:
  96:

 103: - Memory/03_chat_logs/2026-03-14_09-30.md
 104: 
 105: Notes:
 106: - memorytree-only change

 108: ```

 110: ## PR Guidance
 111: 
 112: - Reuse the commit title as the PR title when it still describes the change accurately.
 113: - Keep the PR scoped to MemoryTree-owned files only.
 114: - State whether the PR is MemoryTree-only and whether auto-merge was enabled.
 115: - State whether raw transcripts were included or intentionally left unstaged in the repo mirror.
 116: - Follow the repository's required target branch, review policy, and CI gates.
 117: 
 118: ## Optional CI Optimization For MemoryTree-Only PRs
 119: 
 120: - If the repository owner explicitly approves it, MemoryTree-only PRs may use lighter CI for `Memory/**` and managed `AGENTS.md` changes.
 121: - Prefer repo-native path filters or dedicated lightweight workflows over disabling CI wholesale.
 122: - Keep branch protection and required checks coherent with the repository's governance model. Do not silently remove protections just to make MemoryTree PRs merge faster.
 123: - If the repository still requires full CI or E2E for documentation-only PRs, follow that stricter rule.
 124: - Ask the user before creating or editing workflow files, path filters, or required-check settings for this optimization.
 125: 
 126: ## Stop And Ask
 127: 
 128: Stop and ask the user before committing, pushing, or opening a PR when any of these are true:
 129: 
 130: 1. The diff touches product code or files outside the MemoryTree whitelist.
 131: 2. `AGENTS.md` has user-managed policy content that cannot be safely merged automatically.
 132: 3. The target branch, base branch, or PR destination is unclear.
 133: 4. The repository forbids bot pushes, automated PRs, or auto-merge.
 134: 5. The repository's review or CI rules conflict with the default MemoryTree-only flow.
 135: 6. Raw transcript upload permission for the repository is unknown.
 136: 7. The diff includes raw transcripts or cleaned transcript indexes from other projects.

   1: # Heartbeat Scheduling
   2: 
   3: Use this file when MemoryTree needs to automate transcript import, cleaning, and push without human intervention or model tokens.
   4: 
   5: ## Goal
   6: 
   7: Complete transcript discovery, import, cleaning, commit, and push without consuming model tokens or requiring human intervention.
   8: 
   9: ## Core Rules
  10: 
  11: 1. `heartbeat.py` executes once and exits. It is stateless and idempotent — safe to re-run at any interval.
  12: 2. The OS-native scheduler invokes `heartbeat.py` on a fixed interval. Use cron (Linux), launchd (macOS), or Task Scheduler (Windows).
  13: 3. One computer runs exactly one scheduled heartbeat task. Multiple registrations on the same machine are not supported.
  14: 4. Each execution scans all three supported client directories (Codex, Claude Code, Gemini CLI).
  15: 5. Each execution follows the sequence: scan → incremental import → clean → commit + push → exit.
  16: 6. The `memorytree-daemon watch` mode (continuous loop) exists only for development and debugging. Production use must rely on the OS scheduler.
  17: 
  18: ## Daemon CLI
  19: 
  20: The `memorytree-daemon` command manages the heartbeat lifecycle:
  21: 
  22: | Subcommand  | Description |
  23: |-------------|-------------|
  24: | `install`   | Register the heartbeat task with the OS scheduler at the configured interval. Refuses to overwrite an existing registration. |
  25: | `uninstall` | Remove the heartbeat task from the OS scheduler. |
  26: | `run-once`  | Execute a single heartbeat cycle immediately, then exit. |
  27: | `watch`     | Run a continuous loop for development and debugging only. |
  28: | `status`    | Show whether a heartbeat task is registered and its last execution result. |
  29: 
  30: ## OS Scheduler Integration
  31: 
  32: `memorytree-daemon install` detects the current platform and registers the heartbeat using the native scheduler:
  33: 
  34: ### Linux (cron)
  35: 
  36: ```text
  37: */5 * * * * /path/to/python /path/to/heartbeat.py >> ~/.memorytree/logs/heartbeat-cron.log 2>&1
  38: ```
  39: 
  40: Detection: check for existing entry with `crontab -l | grep memorytree`.
  41: Removal: `crontab -l | grep -v memorytree | crontab -`.
  42: 
  43: ### macOS (launchd)
  44: 
  45: Write a plist to `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.memorytree.heartbeat.plist`:
  46: 
  47: ```xml
  48: <key>ProgramArguments</key>
  49: <array>
  50:   <string>/path/to/python</string>
  51:   <string>/path/to/heartbeat.py</string>
  52: </array>
  53: <key>StartInterval</key>
  54: <integer>300</integer>
  55: ```
  56: 
  57: Load with `launchctl load`, unload with `launchctl unload`.
  58: 
  59: ### Windows (Task Scheduler)
  60: 
  61: ```text
  62: schtasks /create /tn "MemoryTree Heartbeat" /sc minute /mo 5 /tr "python heartbeat.py" /f
  63: ```
  64: 
  65: Detection: `schtasks /query /tn "MemoryTree Heartbeat"`.
  66: Removal: `schtasks /delete /tn "MemoryTree Heartbeat" /f`.
  67: 
  68: ## Execution Flow
  69: 
  70: 1. Acquire `~/.memorytree/heartbeat.lock`. If the lock is held by a live process, exit immediately.
  71: 2. Load `~/.memorytree/config.toml`. If the file is missing or malformed, use built-in defaults and log a warning.
  72: 3. Iterate over registered projects in `config.toml`.
  73: 4. For each project: discover new transcripts → import → clean → commit. If any step fails for one project, log the error, write an alert, and continue to the next project. Never abort the entire heartbeat run because of a single project failure.
  74: 5. If `auto_push = true` and a Git remote exists, push. If the push fails, retry once. On second failure, write an alert and continue.
  75: 6. Release the lock and exit.
  76: 
  77: ## Lock Mechanism
  78: 
  79: The heartbeat uses a PID-based lock file at `~/.memorytree/heartbeat.lock`:
  80: 
  81: 1. On startup, check if the lock file exists.
  82: 2. If it exists, read the PID from the file. Check whether that PID is still alive (`os.kill(pid, 0)` on Unix, `OpenProcess` on Windows).
  83: 3. If the PID is alive, the lock is held — exit immediately with a `lock_held` alert.
  84: 4. If the PID is not alive (stale lock from a crashed process), delete the lock file, log a warning, and proceed.
  85: 5. Write the current PID to the lock file.
  86: 6. On exit (normal or error), always delete the lock file. Use `try/finally` to ensure cleanup.
  87: 
  88: ## Error Handling
  89: 
  90: - **Per-project isolation**: A failure in one project must not prevent other projects from being processed. Catch exceptions at the project level, log the error, write an alert, and continue.
  91: - **Failure threshold**: After 3 consecutive failures for the same project across heartbeat runs, write a `push_failed` or relevant alert to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`. The count resets on a successful run.
  92: - **Config errors**: If `config.toml` contains invalid values (e.g., negative interval, non-existent path), use built-in defaults for those fields and log a warning. Do not abort.
  93: - **Git errors**: If `git add` or `git commit` fails, skip the push for that project and write an alert. Do not attempt to push uncommitted state.
  94: 
  95: ## Sensitive Info Scanning
  96: 
  97: During the cleaning step, scan each transcript for patterns that match API keys, passwords, tokens, and other secrets. When a match is found:
  98: 
  99: - Log a warning with the file path and match location.
 100: - Write an alert to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`.
 101: - Do **not** automatically delete or redact the content.
 102: 
 103: The user reviews alerts and decides how to handle sensitive content.
 104: 
 105: ## Git Remote Pre-Check
 106: 
 107: Before pushing, verify that the target repository has a configured Git remote:
 108: 
 109: - If a remote exists, push the current branch.
 110: - If no remote is configured, skip the push, log a warning, and write an alert to `~/.memorytree/alerts.json`.
 111: 
 112: ## First Install
 113: 
 114: When the skill activates for the first time and `memorytree-daemon` is not registered, use an interactive prompt to configure the heartbeat before installing. Ask the user for:
 115: 
 116: 1. Heartbeat interval (default: 5 minutes).
 117: 2. Whether `auto_push` should be enabled (default: true).
 118: 3. Confirmation of the project scope (which directories to scan).
 119: 
 120: After confirmation, run `memorytree-daemon install` with the chosen settings.
 121: 
 122: The prompt must use plain-text questions and wait for the user's reply. Do not rely on client-specific UI components (buttons, checkboxes, multi-select widgets) — the same prompt must work in Claude Code, Codex, and Gemini CLI.
 123: 
 124: Do not register the heartbeat task silently during initialization.
 125: 
 126: ## On-Demand Sync
 127: 
 128: When the user asks to see their most recent conversation (e.g., "look at my last chat"), trigger an immediate sync instead of waiting for the next scheduled heartbeat:
 129: 
 130: 1. Scan all three client transcript directories for the current project.
 131: 2. Incrementally import any new transcripts into the global archive and project mirror.
 132: 3. Query the global index (`sessions.jsonl` / `search.sqlite`) with `project = current directory`, sorted by timestamp descending.
 133: 4. Exclude the current session: record the skill activation timestamp when the session starts. Any transcript with `started_at` >= activation timestamp is considered the current session and excluded. This approach is cross-client and does not require knowing client-specific session IDs.
 134: 5. If no matching previous session is found, inform the user: "No previous session found for this project." Do not generate a summary.
 135: 6. Load the matched transcript and generate a continuation summary using model tokens.
 136: 
 137: The continuation summary should extract:
 138: 
 139: - What problem was being discussed.
 140: - What approaches were tried.
 141: - How far the work progressed.
 142: - What remains unresolved and where it got stuck.
 143: 
 144: This path is distinct from the scheduled heartbeat: it is user-triggered, immediate, scoped to one project, and produces a model-generated summary. The scheduled heartbeat is background-only and never consumes model tokens.
 145: 
 146: See `references/transcript-archive.md` for the session continuity search flow.
 147: 
 148: ## Stop And Ask
 149: 
 150: Stop and ask the user before proceeding when any of these are true:
 151: 
 152: 1. The `install` subcommand would register a new OS-level scheduled task. Confirm the interval, auto_push preference, and scope first.
 153: 2. A push target has no configured Git remote.
 154: 3. An existing heartbeat registration would be overwritten by a new `install`.
 155: 
 156: ## Cross-Client Compatibility
 157: 
 158: All interactive prompts in this skill (heartbeat install, configuration, on-demand sync confirmation) must work across every AI assistant that supports the skill:
 159: 
 160: 1. Use plain-text questions and wait for the user's text reply. Do not use client-specific UI components.
 161: 2. Follow the user's language or the repo locale for prompt text. Do not hardcode a single language.
 162: 3. Keep script CLI interfaces uniform regardless of which client invokes them.

Expand full message

不是“skill 本身导致了 SSH 失败”，但它现在的实现体验确实可以优化，而且很适合提一个 issue，甚至提 PR。

更准确地说：

- 根因是你仓库的 push URL 是 ssh://git@ssh.github.com:443/beyondchenlin/clonecut.git，而这台机器对这个 SSH 主机没有通过校验，所以 git push -u 失败了。
- 这不是提示词层面的 skill 决策错误。
- 但 memorytree 的 quick-start/CLI 在这里做得不够友好，所以“可以改进”这点是成立的。

我看了实现，当前逻辑是：

- quick-start 会调用注册流程，然后在 auto_push=true 时直接尝试 git push -u 建 upstream，见 [cmd-daemon.ts](C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/cmd-daemon.ts#L210) 和 [cmd-daemon.ts](C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/memorytree-workflow/src/cli/cmd-daemon.ts#L214)
- 真正的 upstream 逻辑只是“找 remote 然后 push”，没有做 SSH/host key 的专项预检查，见 [worktree.ts](C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/memorytree-workflow/src/heartbeat/worktree.ts#L83)
- 文档里其实写了“首次 push 前要确认 remote 和 branch 是否正确”，见 [git-policy.md](C:/Users/ai/.codex/skills/memorytree-workflow/references/git-policy.md#L47)
- 但实现里目前没有这层确认或更友好的诊断

所以我的判断是：

- 不是“功能 bug”意义上的错，因为环境真的没配好
- 是“UX / error handling / preflight check 不足”的问题
- 很适合提 issue
- 如果你们愿意，也完全值得提 PR

比较值得提的优化点有这几个：

1. 在首次 push 前显示实际使用的 push URL
现在用户只能看到 origin/memorytree，但不知道它实际走的是 HTTPS 还是 SSH，像你这种 fetch 用 HTTPS、push 用 SSH 的情况很容易误判。

2. 对常见 SSH 错误做更友好的解释
比如捕获 Host key verification failed 后，明确提示：
“当前 push URL 使用 SSH；请为 ssh.github.com:443 配置 known_hosts，或改用 HTTPS push URL。”

3. 把“本地注册成功”和“远端 upstream 配置失败”分开汇报
你这次其实本地注册和 worktree 创建已经成功了，但输出看起来像整个 quick-start 都失败了。这个很容易让人误解。

4. 给首次接入增加 preflight
在真正 git push -u 前先检查：
- 是否存在 push remote
- push URL 是什么
- 是 HTTPS 还是 SSH
- 如果是 SSH，是否可能走到非默认 host/port

我建议 issue 标题可以这样写：

daemon quick-start should preflight push remote and show actionable SSH host-key errors

issue 核心内容可以写成：

- 当前行为：quick-start 在 auto_push=true 时直接执行 git push -u，SSH host key 问题只返回原始 Git 错误
- 问题：用户不知道实际 push URL，也不知道本地注册是否已经成功
- 期望：
- 输出 push URL
- 对 Host key verification failed 给出可操作提示
- 明确区分“project registered locally”与“upstream not configured”
- 首次 push 前做 remote/protocol preflight

如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接帮你把这个 issue 文案写好，或者我也可以基于这个 skill 仓库直接起一个 PR 方案草稿。

/**
 * Subprocess execution wrapper for git and other commands.
 * Port of heartbeat.py _git() and daemon subprocess calls.
 */

import { execFileSync } from 'node:child_process'

export function execCommand(
  command: string,
  args: readonly string[],
  options?: { cwd?: string; timeout?: number; allowFailure?: boolean },
): string {
  const cwd = options?.cwd
  const timeout = options?.timeout ?? 120_000
  const allowFailure = options?.allowFailure ?? false

  try {
    const stdout = execFileSync(command, [...args], {
      cwd,
      timeout,
      encoding: 'utf-8',
      stdio: ['pipe', 'pipe', 'pipe'],
    })
    return stdout
  } catch (err: unknown) {
    if (allowFailure) {
      const e = err as { stdout?: string }
      return typeof e.stdout === 'string' ? e.stdout : ''
    }
    throw err
  }
}

export function git(cwd: string, ...args: string[]): string {
  const allowFailure = args[0] === 'status' || args[0] === 'remote'
  return execCommand('git', args, { cwd, allowFailure })
}
